Unfortunately\n123:         # the end result is that it is impossible to force the query to have\n124:         # a chosen GROUP BY clause - you can almost do this by using the form:\n125:         #     .values(*wanted_cols).annotate(AnAggregate())\n126:         # but any later annotations, extra selects, values calls that\n127:         # refer some column outside of the wanted_cols, order_by, or even\n128:         # filter calls can alter the GROUP BY clause.\n129: \n130:         # The query.group_by is either None (no GROUP BY at all), True\n131:         # (group by select fields), or a list of expressions to be added\n132:         # to the group by.\n133:         if self.query.group_by is None:\n134:             return []\n135:         expressions = []\n136:         group_by_refs = set()\n137:         if self.query.group_by is not True:\n138:             # If the group by is set to a list (by .values() call most likely),\n139:             # then we need to add everything in it to the GROUP BY clause.\n140:             # Backwards compatibility hack for setting query.group_by. The\n1597:         return value depends on the value of result_type.\n1598: \n1599:         When result_type is:\n1600:         - MULTI: Retrieves all rows using fetchmany(). Wraps in an iterator for\n1601:            chunked reads when supported.\n1602:         - SINGLE: Retrieves a single row using fetchone().\n1603:         - ROW_COUNT: Retrieves the number of rows in the result.\n1604:         - CURSOR: Runs the query, and returns the cursor object. Check for raw values,\n1685:         expressions, and fields with get_placeholder() defined in that order.\n1686: \n1687:         When field is None, consider the value raw and use it as the\n1688:         placeholder, with no corresponding parameters returned.\n1689:         \"\"\"\n1690:         if field is None:\n1691:             # A field value of None means the value is raw.\n1692:             sql, params = val, []\n1693:         elif hasattr(val, \"as_sql\"):\n1694:             # This is an expression, let's compile it.\n1695:             sql, params = self.compile(val)\n1696:         elif get_placeholder is not None:\n1697:             # Some fields (e.g. geo fields) need special munging before\n1698:             # they can be inserted.\n1699:             sql, params = get_placeholder(val, self, self.connection), [val]\n1700:         else:\n1701:             # Return the common case for the placeholder\n1702:             sql, params = \"%s\", [val]\n1703: \n1704:         # The following hook is only used by Oracle Spatial, which sometimes\n1705:         # needs to yield 'NULL' and [] as its placeholder and params instead\n1706:         # of '%s' and [None].               str(Person.objects.filter(name=\\\"foo\\\").select_for_update().query),\\n491:                 )\\n492: \\n493:     @skipUnlessDBFeature(\\\"has_select_for_update\\\", \\\"supports_transactions\\\")\\n494:     def test_for_update_requires_transaction(self):\\n495:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n496:         A TransactionManagementError is raised\\n497:         when a @skipUnlessDBFeature(\\\"has_select_for_update\\\", \\\"supports_transactions\\\")\\n504:     def test_for_update_requires_transaction_only_in_execution(self):\\n505:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n506:         No TransactionManagementError is raised\\n507:         when select_for_update is invoked outside of a transaction -\\n508:         only when the query is executed.\\n509:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n510:         people = Person.objects.select_for_update()\\n511:         msg = \\\"select_for_update cannot be used outside of a transaction.\\\"\\n512:         with self.assertRaisesMessage(transaction.TransactionManagementError, msg):\\n513:             list(people)\\n514: \\n515:     @skipUnlessDBFeature(\\\"supports_select_for_update_with_limit\\\")\\n516:     def test_select_for_update_with_limit(self):\\n517:         other = Person.objects.create(name=\\\"Grappeli\\\", born=self.city1, died=self.city2)\\n518:         with transaction.atomic():\\n519:             qs = list(Person.objects.order_by(\\\"pk\\\").select_for_update()[1:2])\\n520:             self.assertEqual(qs[0], other)\\n521: \\n522:     @skipIfDBFeature(\\\"supports_select_for_update_with_limit\\\")\\n523:     def test_unsupported_select_for_update_with_limit(self):\\n524:         msg = (\\n525:             \\\"LIMIT/OFFSET is not supported with select_for_update on this database \\\"\\n526:             \\\"backend.\\\"\\n527:         )\\n528:         with self.assertRaisesMessage(NotSupportedError, msg):\\n529:             with transaction.atomic():\\n530:                 list(Person.objects.order_by(\\\"pk\\\").select_for_update()[1:2])\\n531: \\n532:     def run_select_for_update(self, status, **kwargs):\\n533:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n534:         Utility method that runs a SELECT FOR UPDATE against all\\n535:         Person instances. After the select_for_update, it attempts\\n536:         to update the name of the only record, save, and commit.\\n537: \\n538:         This function expects to run in a separate thread.\\n539:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n540:         status.append(\\\"started\\\")\\n541:         try:\\n542:             # We need to enter transaction management again, as this is done on\\n543:             # per-thread basis\\n544:             with transaction.atomic():\\n545:                 person = Person.objects.select_for_update(**kwargs).get()\\n546:                 person.name = \\\"Fred\\\"\\n547:                 person.save()\\n548:         except (DatabaseError, Person.DoesNotExist) as e:\\n549:             status.append(e)\\n550:         finally:\\n551:             # This method is run in a separate thread. It uses its own\\n552:             # database connection. Close it without waiting for the GC.\\n553:             connection.close()\\n554: \\n555:     @skipUnlessDBFeature(\\\"has_select_for_update\\\")\\n556:     @skipUnlessDBFeature(\\\"supports_transactions\\\")\\n557:     def test_block(self):\\n558:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n559:         A thread running a select_for_update that accesses rows being touched\\n560:         by a similar operation on another connection blocks correctly.\\n561:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n562:         # First, let's start the transaction in our thread.\\n563:         self.start_blocking_transaction()\\n564: \\n565:         # Now, try it again using the ORM's select_for_update\\n566:         # facility. Do this in a separate thread.\\n567:         status = []\\n568:         thread = threading.Thread(target=self.run_select_for_update, args=(status,))\\n569: \\n570:         # The thread should immediately block, but we'll sleep\\n571:         # for a bit to make sure.\\n572:         thread.start()\\n573:         sanity_count = 0\\n574:         while len(status) != 1 and sanity_count < 10:\\n575:             sanity_count += 1\\n576:             time.sleep(1)\\n577:         if sanity_count >= 10:\\n578:             raise ValueError(\\\"Thread did not run and block\\\")\\n579: \\n580:         # Check the person hasn't been updated. Since this isn't\\n581:         # using FOR UPDATE, it won't block.\\n582:         p = Person.objects.get(pk=self.person.pk)\\n583:         self.assertEqual(\\\"Reinhardt\\\", p.name)\\n584: \\n585:         # When we end our blocking transaction, our thread should\\n586:         # be able to continue.\\n587:         self.end_blocking_transaction()\\n588:         thread.join(5.0)\\n589: \\n590:         # Check the thread has finished.  \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n534:         Utility method that runs a SELECT FOR UPDATE against all\\n535:         Person instances. After the select_for_update, it attempts\\n536:         to update the name of the only record, save, and commit.\\n537: \\n538:         This function expects to run in a separate thread.\\n539:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n540:         status.append(\\\"started\\\")\\n541:         try:\\n542:             # We need to enter transaction management again, as this is done on\\n543:             # per-thread basis\\n544:             with transaction.atomic():\\n545:                 person = Person.objects.select_for_update(**kwargs).get()\\n546:                 person.name = \\\"Fred\\\"\\n547:                 person.save()\\n548:         except (DatabaseError, Person.DoesNotExist) as e:\\n549:             status.append(e)\\n550:         finally:\\n551:             # This method is run in a separate thread. Close it without waiting for the GC.\\n553:             connection.close()\\n554: \\n555:     @skipUnlessDBFeature(\\\"has_select_for_update\\\")\\n556:     @skipUnlessDBFeature(\\\"supports_transactions\\\")\\n557:     def test_block(self):\\n558:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n559:         A thread running a select_for_update that accesses rows being touched\\n560:         by a similar operation on another connection blocks correctly.\\n561:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n562:         # First, let's start the transaction in our thread.\\n563:         self.start_blocking_transaction()\\n564: \\n565:         # Now, try it again using the ORM's select_for_update\\n566:         # facility. Do this in a separate thread.\\n567:         status = []\\n568:         thread = threading.Thread(target=self.run_select_for_update, args=(status,))\\n569: \\n570:         # The thread should immediately block, but we'll sleep\\n571:         # for a bit to make sure.\\n572:         thread.start()\\n573:         sanity_count = 0\\n574:         while len(status) != 1 and sanity_count < 10:\\n575:             sanity_count += 1\\n576:             time.sleep(1)\\n577:         if sanity_count >= 10:\\n578:             raise ValueError(\\\"Thread did not run and block\\\")\\n579: \\n580:         # Check the person hasn't been updated. Since this isn't\\n581:         # using FOR UPDATE, it won't block.\\n582:         p = Person.objects.get(pk=self.person.pk)\\n583:         self.assertEqual(\\\"Reinhardt\\\", p.name)\\n584: \\n585:         # When we end our blocking transaction, our thread should\\n586:         # be able to continue.\\n587:         self.end_blocking_transaction()\\n588:         thread.join(5.0)\\n589: \\n590:         # Check the thread has finished. Assuming it has, we should\\n591:         # find that it has updated the person's name.\\n592:         self.assertFalse(thread.is_alive())\\n593: \\n594:         # We must commit the transaction to ensure that MySQL gets a fresh read,\\n595:         # since by default it runs in REPEATABLE READ mode\\n596:         transaction.commit()\\n597: \\n598:         p = Person.objects.get(pk=self.person.pk)\\n599:         self.assertEqual(\\\"Fred\\\", p.name)\\n600: \\n601:     @skipUnlessDBFeature(\\\"has_select_for_update\\\", \\\"supports_transactions\\\")\\n602:     def test_raw_lock_not_available(self):\\n603:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n604:         Running a raw query which can't obtain a FOR UPDATE lock raises\\n605:         the correct exception\\n606:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n607:         self.start_blocking_transaction()\\n608: \\n609:         def raw(status):\\n610:             try:\\n611:                 list(\\n612:                     Person.objects.raw(\\n613:                         \\\"SELECT * FROM %s %s\\\"\\n614:                         % (\\n615:                             Person._meta.db_table,\\n616:                             connection.ops.for_update_sql(nowait=True),\\n617:                         )\\n618:                     )\\n619:                 )\\n620:             except DatabaseError as e:\\n621:                 status.append(e)\\n622:             finally:\\n623:                 # This method is run in a separate thread. Crash with Annotation Expressions - Bug Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — examined for `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method and the buggy `.target.model` access\n- `django/db/models/sql/query.py` — examined for `set_values()` method to understand how `values_list()` builds the SELECT list\n- `django/db/models/query.py` — examined for `values_list()` method to understand user-facing API\n- `django/db/models/expressions.py` — examined to understand the `Col` class and `.target` attribute\n- `tests/select_for_update/tests.py` — examined for existing test coverage\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: User code\n   - Queryset: `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n   - Error: `AttributeError` on accessing `.target.model`\n\n2. **Called from**: `SQLCompiler.get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` line 1405\n   - Called during SQL compilation to generate the `FOR UPDATE OF` clause\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: Line 1424 and line 1440 in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n   - Tries to access `.target.model` on all items in `self.select`\n   - Fails when items are annotation expressions (which don't have `.target`)\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Functions**:\n  - `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (line 1405)\n    - Nested function `_get_parent_klass_info()` (line 1411)\n    - Nested function `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` (line 1430)\n\n- **Line(s)**:\n  - Line 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info`)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model`)\n\n- **Explanation**:\n\nThe bug occurs because the `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method assumes that every item in `self.select` is a `Col` expression object with a `.target` attribute. However, when `values_list()` is combined with annotation expressions, the SELECT list can contain non-`Col` expressions (like `Concat`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) that don't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n### How the bug manifests:\n\n1. When `values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")` is called, it creates annotation expressions\n2. The `_values()` method calls `annotate()` to register the annotation\n3. Then `set_values()` in `Query` builds a `selected` dictionary that preserves the order of fields as passed to `values_list()`\n4. In `get_select()` of `SQLCompiler`, when `self.query.selected` is not None, it builds the `select` list by iterating through `selected.items()`, which means annotations can appear before model field columns\n5. When `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` is called, it tries to access `.target.model` on items in `self.select`\n6. If an annotation expression is at index 0 (or any position before model fields), accessing `.target` raises an `AttributeError`\n\n### Why this wasn't caught before:\n\nPrior to the `values()`/`values_list()` field ordering change, model field columns were always placed first in the SELECT clause (before annotations). This meant that when looking for model fields by checking `.target.model`, the code would always find them at the expected positions. The bug only manifests when annotations can appear before model field columns in the SELECT list.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n```diff\n--- a/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n+++ b/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n@@ -1420,8 +1420,10 @@ class SQLCompiler(BaseSQL):\n                     \"select_fields\": [\n                         select_index\n                         for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                         # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n-                        if (\n+                        if (hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                            and (\n                             self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n                             or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n-                        )\n+                            )\n+                        )\n                     ],\n                 }\n\n@@ -1437,7 +1439,8 @@ class SQLCompiler(BaseSQL):\n             \"\"\"\n             concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n             for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-                if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+                if (hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                        and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model):\n                     return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Alternative Fix (More Defensive)\n\nUsing `isinstance()` check instead of `hasattr()`:\n\n```diff\nfrom django.db.models.expressions import Col\n\n# In _get_first_selected_col_from_model:\nfor select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n    expr = self.select[select_index][0]\n    if isinstance(expr, Col) and expr.target.model == concrete_model:\n        return expr\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How values_list() builds the SELECT list:\n\n1. `values_list(*fields, **expressions)` in `query.py:1369` takes positional arguments (fields) and keyword arguments (annotations)\n2. It calls `_values(*_fields, **expressions)` where `expressions` are added via `annotate()`\n3. `set_values(fields)` in `query.py:2492` builds the `selected` dictionary:\n   - For each field, it checks if it's an extra, annotation, or regular field\n   - If it's an annotation, it stores the annotation name as a string: `selected[f] = f`\n   - If it's a regular field, it stores the index: `selected[f] = len(field_names)`\n   - The order in `selected` matches the order of fields passed to `values_list()`\n\n4. `get_select()` in `compiler.py:230` processes the `selected` dictionary:\n   ```python\n   for alias, expression in self.query.selected.items():\n       if isinstance(expression, str):\n           expression = self.query.annotations[expression]  # Get the annotation expression\n       elif isinstance(expression, int):\n           expression = cols[expression]  # Get the column\n       selected.append((alias, expression))\n   ```\n   - This preserves the order from `self.query.selected`\n   - If annotations come first in the user's `values_list()` call, they appear first in `selected` and then in `self.select`\n\n### Why the fix works:\n\nThe fix adds a check `hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")` before accessing `.target`. This ensures that:\n\n1. Only `Col` expressions (which represent actual database columns) are considered for `select_for_update(of=...)`\n2. Annotation expressions are safely skipped, as they don't represent model columns that need locking\n3. The method correctly identifies which model fields are present in the SELECT list, regardless of annotation ordering\n\nThis is semantically correct because:\n- `select_for_update(of=(...))` is designed to lock specific tables/models in the database\n- Only `Col` expressions represent actual database columns that need locking\n- Annotations are computed values that don't correspond to specific table columns, so they shouldn't affect which tables are locked\n\n### Testing recommendation:\n\nAdd a test case to `tests/select_for_update/tests.py`:\n```python\n@skipUnlessDBFeature(\"has_select_for_update_of\")\ndef test_for_update_of_with_values_list_annotation(self):\n    \"\"\"\n    select_for_update(of=...) should work correctly when values_list()\n    contains annotation expressions before model fields.\n    \"\"\"\n    with transaction.atomic():\n        # This should not raise AttributeError\n        values = list(\n            Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n                Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"pk\"\n            )\n        )\n    self.assertEqual(len(values), 1)\n    self.assertTrue(values[0][0].startswith(\"Dr. \"))\n```\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2006,"cache_read_input_tokens":72488,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2006},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"285afcb2-3490-4875-892b-40ba4c99bf44","uuid":"0804168f-2383-47fc-829b-7bacd274a7ca"}

However, when `values_list()` is combined with annotation expressions, the SELECT list can contain non-`Col` expressions (like `Concat`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) that don't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n### How the bug manifests:\n\n1. When `values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")` is called, it creates annotation expressions\n2. The `_values()` method calls `annotate()` to register the annotation\n3. Then `set_values()` in `Query` builds a `selected` dictionary that preserves the order of fields as passed to `values_list()`\n4. In `get_select()` of `SQLCompiler`, when `self.query.selected` is not None, it builds the `select` list by iterating through `selected.items()`, which means annotations can appear before model field columns\n5. When `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` is called, it tries to access `.target.model` on items in `self.select`\n6. If an annotation expression is at index 0 (or any position before model fields), accessing `.target` raises an `AttributeError`\n\n### Why this wasn't caught before:\n\nPrior to the `values()`/`values_list()` field ordering change, model field columns were always placed first in the SELECT clause (before annotations). This meant that when looking for model fields by checking `.target.model`, the code would always find them at the expected positions. The bug only manifests when annotations can appear before model field columns in the SELECT list.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n```diff\n--- a/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n+++ b/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n@@ -1420,8 +1420,10 @@ class SQLCompiler(BaseSQL):\n                     \"select_fields\": [\n                         select_index\n                         for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                         # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n-                        if (\n+                        if (hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                            and (\n                             self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n                             or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n-                        )\n+                            )\n+                        )\n                     ],\n                 }\n\n@@ -1437,7 +1439,8 @@ class SQLCompiler(BaseSQL):\n             \"\"\"\n             concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n             for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-                if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+                if (hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                        and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model):\n                     return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Alternative Fix (More Defensive)\n\nUsing `isinstance()` check instead of `hasattr()`:\n\n```diff\nfrom django.db.models.expressions import Col\n\n# In _get_first_selected_col_from_model:\nfor select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n    expr = self.select[select_index][0]\n    if isinstance(expr, Col) and expr.target.model == concrete_model:\n        return expr\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How values_list() builds the SELECT list:\n\n1. `values_list(*fields, **expressions)` in `query.py:1369` takes positional arguments (fields) and keyword arguments (annotations)\n2. It calls `_values(*_fields, **expressions)` where `expressions` are added via `annotate()`\n3. `set_values(fields)` in `query.py:2492` builds the `selected` dictionary:\n   - For each field, it checks if it's an extra, annotation, or regular field\n   - If it's an annotation, it stores the annotation name as a string: `selected[f] = f`\n   - If it's a regular field, it stores the index: `selected[f] = len(field_names)`\n   - The order in `selected` matches the order of fields passed to `values_list()`\n\n4. `get_select()` in `compiler.py:230` processes the `selected` dictionary:\n   ```python\n   for alias, expression in self.query.selected.items():\n       if isinstance(expression, str):\n           expression = self.query.annotations[expression]  # Get the annotation expression\n       elif isinstance(expression, int):\n           expression = cols[expression]  # Get the column\n       selected.append((alias, expression))\n   ```\n   - This preserves the order from `self.query.selected`\n   - If annotations come first in the user's `values_list()` call, they appear first in `selected` and then in `self.select`\n\n### Why the fix works:\n\nThe fix adds a check `hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")` before accessing `.target`. This ensures that:\n\n1. Only `Col` expressions (which represent actual database columns) are considered for `select_for_update(of=...)`\n2. Annotation expressions are safely skipped, as they don't represent model columns that need locking\n3. The method correctly identifies which model fields are present in the SELECT list, regardless of annotation ordering\n\nThis is semantically correct because:\n- `select_for_update(of=(...))` is designed to lock specific tables/models in the database\n- Only `Col` expressions represent actual database columns that need locking\n- Annotations are computed values that don't correspond to specific table columns, so they shouldn't affect which tables are locked\n\n### Testing recommendation:\n\nAdd a test case to `tests/select_for_update/tests.py`:\n```python\n@skipUnlessDBFeature(\"has_select_for_update_of\")\ndef test_for_update_of_with_values_list_annotation(self):\n    \"\"\"\n    select_for_update(of=...) should work correctly when values_list()\n    contains annotation expressions before model fields.\n    \"\"\"\n    with transaction.atomic():\n        # This should not raise AttributeError\n        values = list(\n            Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n                Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"pk\"\n            )\n        )\n    self.assertEqual(len(values), 1)\n    self.assertTrue(values[0][0].startswith(\"Dr. \"))\n```\n\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":80,"oldLines":11,"newStart":80,"newLines":25,"lines":["                      return self.select[select_index][0]"," ```"," ","-## Alternative Fix (More Defensive)","+## Justification for Using hasattr() Check"," ","+The proposed fix using `hasattr(expr, \"target\")` is consistent with existing Django code in the same file. Crash with Annotation Expressions - Bug Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — examined for `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method and the buggy `.target.model` access\n- `django/db/models/sql/query.py` — examined for `set_values()` method to understand how `values_list()` builds the SELECT list\n- `django/db/models/query.py` — examined for `values_list()` method to understand user-facing API\n- `django/db/models/expressions.py` — examined to understand the `Col` class and `.target` attribute\n- `tests/select_for_update/tests.py` — examined for existing test coverage\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: User code\n   - Queryset: `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n   - Error: `AttributeError` on accessing `.target.model`\n\n2. **Called from**: `SQLCompiler.get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` line 1405\n   - Called during SQL compilation to generate the `FOR UPDATE OF` clause\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: Line 1424 and line 1440 in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n   - Tries to access `.target.model` on all items in `self.select`\n   - Fails when items are annotation expressions (which don't have `.target`)\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Functions**:\n  - `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (line 1405)\n    - Nested function `_get_parent_klass_info()` (line 1411)\n    - Nested function `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` (line 1430)\n\n- **Line(s)**:\n  - Line 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info`)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model`)\n\n- **Explanation**:\n\nThe bug occurs because the `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method assumes that every item in `self.select` is a `Col` expression object with a `.target` attribute. However, when `values_list()` is combined with annotation expressions, the SELECT list can contain non-`Col` expressions (like `Concat`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) that don't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n### How the bug manifests:\n\n1. When `values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")` is called, it creates annotation expressions\n2. The `_values()` method calls `annotate()` to register the annotation\n3. Then `set_values()` in `Query` builds a `selected` dictionary that preserves the order of fields as passed to `values_list()`\n4. In `get_select()` of `SQLCompiler`, when `self.query.selected` is not None, it builds the `select` list by iterating through `selected.items()`, which means annotations can appear before model field columns\n5. When `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` is called, it tries to access `.target.model` on items in `self.select`\n6. If an annotation expression is at index 0 (or any position before model fields), accessing `.target` raises an `AttributeError`\n\n### Why this wasn't caught before:\n\nPrior to the `values()`/`values_list()` field ordering change, model field columns were always placed first in the SELECT clause (before annotations). This meant that when looking for model fields by checking `.target.model`, the code would always find them at the expected positions. The bug only manifests when annotations can appear before model field columns in the SELECT list.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n```diff\n--- a/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n+++ b/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n@@ -1420,8 +1420,10 @@ class SQLCompiler(BaseSQL):\n                     \"select_fields\": [\n                         select_index\n                         for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                         # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n-                        if (\n+                        if (hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                            and (\n                             self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n                             or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n-                        )\n+                            )\n+                        )\n                     ],\n                 }\n\n@@ -1437,7 +1439,8 @@ class SQLCompiler(BaseSQL):\n             \"\"\"\n             concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n             for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-                if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+                if (hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                        and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model):\n                     return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Justification for Using hasattr() Check\n\nThe proposed fix using `hasattr(expr, \"target\")` is consistent with existing Django code in the same file. At line 213 in the GROUP BY logic, the code already uses:\n\n```python\nhasattr(expr, \"target\")\nand expr.target.primary_key\n```\n\nThis confirms that:\n1. The `hasattr()` approach is the established pattern in Django for handling mixed expression types\n2. The fix is consistent with the codebase's defensive programming practices\n3. Expressions can have or not have a `.target` attribute, and both cases must be handled\n\n## Alternative Fix (Using isinstance)\n\nUsing `isinstance()` check instead of `hasattr()`:\n\n```python\nfrom django.db.models.expressions import Col\n\n# In _get_first_selected_col_from_model:\nfor select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n    expr = self.select[select_index][0]\n    if isinstance(expr, Col) and expr.target.model == concrete_model:\n        return expr\n```\n\nHowever, the `hasattr()` approach is preferred because:\n1. It's already established in this file at line 213\n2. It's more flexible if other expression types with `.target` are added in the future\n3. It doesn't require importing `Col`\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How values_list() builds the SELECT list:\n\n1. `values_list(*fields, **expressions)` in `query.py:1369` takes positional arguments (fields) and keyword arguments (annotations)\n2. It calls `_values(*_fields, **expressions)` where `expressions` are added via `annotate()`\n3. `set_values(fields)` in `query.py:2492` builds the `selected` dictionary:\n   - For each field, it checks if it's an extra, annotation, or regular field\n   - If it's an annotation, it stores the annotation name as a string: `selected[f] = f`\n   - If it's a regular field, it stores the index: `selected[f] = len(field_names)`\n   - The order in `selected` matches the order of fields passed to `values_list()`\n\n4. `get_select()` in `compiler.py:230` processes the `selected` dictionary:\n   ```python\n   for alias, expression in self.query.selected.items():\n       if isinstance(expression, str):\n           expression = self.query.annotations[expression]  # Get the annotation expression\n       elif isinstance(expression, int):\n           expression = cols[expression]  # Get the column\n       selected.append((alias, expression))\n   ```\n   - This preserves the order from `self.query.selected`\n   - If annotations come first in the user's `values_list()` call, they appear first in `selected` and then in `self.select`\n\n### Why the fix works:\n\nThe fix adds a check `hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")` before accessing `.target`. This ensures that:\n\n1. Only `Col` expressions (which represent actual database columns) are considered for `select_for_update(of=...)`\n2. Annotation expressions are safely skipped, as they don't represent model columns that need locking\n3. The method correctly identifies which model fields are present in the SELECT list, regardless of annotation ordering\n\nThis is semantically correct because:\n- `select_for_update(of=(...))` is designed to lock specific tables/models in the database\n- Only `Col` expressions represent actual database columns that need locking\n- Annotations are computed values that don't correspond to specific table columns, so they shouldn't affect which tables are locked\n\n### Testing recommendation:\n\nAdd a test case to `tests/select_for_update/tests.py`:\n```python\n@skipUnlessDBFeature(\"has_select_for_update_of\")\ndef test_for_update_of_with_values_list_annotation(self):\n    \"\"\"\n    select_for_update(of=...) should work correctly when values_list()\n    contains annotation expressions before model fields.\n    \"\"\"\n    with transaction.atomic():\n        # This should not raise AttributeError\n        values = list(\n            Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n                Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"pk\"\n            )\n        )\n    self.assertEqual(len(values), 1)\n    self.assertTrue(values[0][0].startswith(\"Dr. \"))\n```\n\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":51,"oldLines":10,"newStart":51,"newLines":54,"lines":[" "," ## Proposed Fix"," ","+The fix adds defensive `hasattr()` checks before accessing `.target` on select expressions. Crash with Annotation Expressions - Bug Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — examined for `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method and the buggy `.target.model` access\n- `django/db/models/sql/query.py` — examined for `set_values()` method to understand how `values_list()` builds the SELECT list\n- `django/db/models/query.py` — examined for `values_list()` method to understand user-facing API\n- `django/db/models/expressions.py` — examined to understand the `Col` class and `.target` attribute\n- `tests/select_for_update/tests.py` — examined for existing test coverage\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: User code\n   - Queryset: `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n   - Error: `AttributeError` on accessing `.target.model`\n\n2. **Called from**: `SQLCompiler.get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` line 1405\n   - Called during SQL compilation to generate the `FOR UPDATE OF` clause\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: Line 1424 and line 1440 in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n   - Tries to access `.target.model` on all items in `self.select`\n   - Fails when items are annotation expressions (which don't have `.target`)\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Functions**:\n  - `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (line 1405)\n    - Nested function `_get_parent_klass_info()` (line 1411)\n    - Nested function `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` (line 1430)\n\n- **Line(s)**:\n  - Line 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info`)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model`)\n\n- **Explanation**:\n\nThe bug occurs because the `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method assumes that every item in `self.select` is a `Col` expression object with a `.target` attribute. However, when `values_list()` is combined with annotation expressions, the SELECT list can contain non-`Col` expressions (like `Concat`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) that don't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n### How the bug manifests:\n\n1. When `values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")` is called, it creates annotation expressions\n2. The `_values()` method calls `annotate()` to register the annotation\n3. Then `set_values()` in `Query` builds a `selected` dictionary that preserves the order of fields as passed to `values_list()`\n4. In `get_select()` of `SQLCompiler`, when `self.query.selected` is not None, it builds the `select` list by iterating through `selected.items()`, which means annotations can appear before model field columns\n5. When `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` is called, it tries to access `.target.model` on items in `self.select`\n6. If an annotation expression is at index 0 (or any position before model fields), accessing `.target` raises an `AttributeError`\n\n### Why this wasn't caught before:\n\nPrior to the `values()`/`values_list()` field ordering change, model field columns were always placed first in the SELECT clause (before annotations). This meant that when looking for model fields by checking `.target.model`, the code would always find them at the expected positions. The bug only manifests when annotations can appear before model field columns in the SELECT list.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix adds defensive `hasattr()` checks before accessing `.target` on select expressions. This ensures that annotation expressions (which don't have `.target`) are safely skipped.\n\n### Change 1: Fix _get_parent_klass_info() (lines 1423-1426)\n\n**Before:**\n```python\nif (\n    self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n    or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n)\n```\n\n**After:**\n```python\nif (\n    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n    and (\n        self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n        or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n    )\n)\n```\n\n### Change 2: Fix _get_first_selected_col_from_model() (lines 1439-1441)\n\n**Before:**\n```python\nfor select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n    if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n        return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n**After:**\n```python\nfor select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n    if (\n        hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n        and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n    ):\n        return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n### Complete Unified Diff\n\n```diff\n--- a/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n+++ b/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n@@ -1420,9 +1420,10 @@ class SQLCompiler(BaseSQL):\n                     \"select_fields\": [\n                         select_index\n                         for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                         # At line 213 in the GROUP BY logic, the code already uses:\n\n```python\nhasattr(expr, \"target\")\nand expr.target.primary_key\n```\n\nThis confirms that:\n1. The `hasattr()` approach is the established pattern in Django for handling mixed expression types\n2. The fix is consistent with the codebase's defensive programming practices\n3. Expressions can have or not have a `.target` attribute, and both cases must be handled\n\n## Alternative Fix (Using isinstance)\n\nUsing `isinstance()` check instead of `hasattr()`:\n\n```python\nfrom django.db.models.expressions import Col\n\n# In _get_first_selected_col_from_model:\nfor select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n    expr = self.select[select_index][0]\n    if isinstance(expr, Col) and expr.target.model == concrete_model:\n        return expr\n```\n\nHowever, the `hasattr()` approach is preferred because:\n1. It doesn't require importing `Col`\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How values_list() builds the SELECT list:\n\n1. `values_list(*fields, **expressions)` in `query.py:1369` takes positional arguments (fields) and keyword arguments (annotations)\n2. However, when `values_list()` is used with annotation expressions (like `Concat()`, `F()`, etc.), these annotations can appear before model field columns in the SELECT list, and annotation expressions don't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n**Specific Problem Lines**:\n- **Line 1424-1425** (in `_get_parent_klass_info()` nested function)\n- **Line 1440** (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` nested function)\n\n**The Fix**: Add defensive `hasattr()` checks before accessing `.target.model`, consistent with existing code patterns in the file (see line 213).\n\nThe analysis includes:\n1.
